          Example 4 in prompt template for generating true statements in statement judging task.
2053
2054      Original Question: The term structure of interest rates is upward sloping. Put the following
2055      in order of magnitude:
2056      (a) The five-year zero rate
2057      (b) The yield on a five-year coupon-bearing bond
2058      (c) The forward rate corresponding to the period between 4.75 and 5 years in the future
2059      What is the answer to this question when the term structure of interest rates is downward
2060      sloping?
2061
2062
          Original Answer: When the term structure is upward sloping, c > a > b. When it
          is downward sloping, b > a > c.
2063
2064
          Context: The term structure of interest rates is upward sloping.
2065
2066      Statement: The five-year zero rate is smaller than the forward rate corresponding to
2067      the period between 4.75 and 5 years in the future.
2068      Answer: True
2069
2070      Statement: The yield on a five-year coupon-bearing bond is smaller than the forward
2071      rate corresponding to the period between 4.75 and 5 years in the future.
2072      Answer: True
2073
          Statement: The yield on a five-year coupon-bearing bond is larger than the five-year
2074
          zero rate.
2075
          Answer: True
2076
2077      Statement: The five-year zero rate is larger than the forward rate corresponding to
2078      the period between 4.75 and 5 years in the future.
2079      Answer: True

2106
          Example 5 in prompt template for generating true statements in statement judging task.
2107
2108      Original Question: For each of the following scenarios, discuss whether profit opportunities
2109      exist from trading in the stock of the firm under the conditions that (1) the market is not
2110      weak form efficient, (2) the market is weak form but not semistrong form efficient, (3) the
2111      market is semistrong form but not strong form efficient, and (4) the market is strong form
2112      efficient. **a.** The stock price has risen steadily each day for the past 30 days. **b.**
2113      The financial statements for a company were released three days ago, and you believe
2114      you’ve uncovered some anomalies in the company’s inventory and cost control reporting
2115      techniques that are causing the firm’s true liquidity strength to be understated. **c.** You
2116
          observe that the senior managers of a company have been buying a lot of the company’s
          stock on the open market over the past week.
2117
2118
          Original Answer:
2119      (a). If the market is not weak form efficient, then this information could be acted on and
2120      a profit earned from following the price trend. Under (2), (3), and (4), this information is
2121      fully impounded in the current price and no abnormal profit opportunity exists.
2122      (b). Under (2), if the market is not semi-strong form efficient, then this information could
2123      be used to buy the stock c̈heapb̈efore the rest of the market discovers the financial statement
2124      anomaly. Since (2) is stronger than (1), both imply that a profit opportunity exists; under (3)
2125      and (4), this information is fully impounded in the current price and no profit opportunity
2126      exists.
2127
          (c). Under (3), if the market is not strong form efficient, then this information could be used
          as a profitable trading strategy, by noting the buying activity of the insiders as a signal that
2128
          the stock is underpriced or that good news is imminent. Since (1) and (2) are weaker than
2129
          (3), all three imply that a profit opportunity exists. Note that this assumes the individual
2130      who sees the insider trading is the only one who sees the trading. If the information about
2131      the trades made by company management is public information, it will be discounted in the
2132      stock price and no profit opportunity exists. Under (4), this information does not signal any
2133      profit opportunity for traders; any pertinent information the manager-insiders may have is
2134      fully reflected in the current share price.
2135
2136      Context: Consider profit opportunities exist from trading in the stock of the firm.
2137
2138
          Statement: In a market that is not weak form efficient, a profit could be earned from
          acting on the information of a stock price that has risen steadily each day for the past 30
2139
          days.
2140
          Answer: True
2141
2142      Statement: In a market that is not semi-strong form efficient, a profit could be earned
2143      from acting on the pertinent information the manager-insiders may have.
2144      Answer: True
2145
2146      Statement: In a market that is not strong form efficient, there is no profit opportunity
2147      on the information that you observe that the senior managers of a company have been
2148      buying a lot of the company’s stock on the open market over the past week.
2149
          Answer: True

          Example 2 in prompt template for generating false statements in statement judging task.
2215
2216      Original Question: What is meant by the delta of a stock option?
2217
2218      Original Answer: The delta of a stock option measures the sensitivity of the option
2219      price to the price of the stock when small changes are considered. Specifically, it is the ratio
2220      of the change in the price of the stock option to the change in the price of the underlying
2221      stock.
2222

2247      Example 3 in prompt template for generating false statements in statement judging task.
2248
          Original Question: The treasurer of a corporation is trying to choose between options and
2249
          forward contracts to hedge the corporation’s foreign exchange risk. Discuss the advantages
2250
          and disadvantages of each.
2251
2252      Original Answer: Forward contracts lock in the exchange rate that will apply to a
2253      particular transaction in the future. Options provide insurance that the exchange rate will
2254      not be worse than some level. The advantage of a forward contract is that uncertainty
2255      is eliminated as far as possible. The disadvantage is that the outcome with hedging
2256      can be significantly worse than the outcome with no hedging. This disadvantage is not
2257      as marked with options. However, unlike forward contracts, options involve an up-front cost.
2258
2259
          Context: The treasurer of a corporation is trying to choose between options and for-
          ward contracts to hedge the corporation’s foreign exchange risk.
2260
2261
          Statement: When using forward contracts for hedging, the outcome is definitely bet-
2262      ter than the outcome with no hedging.
2263      Answer: False
2264
2265      Statement: Using forward contracts to hedge the foreign exchange risk involve an
2266      up-front cost.
2267      Answer: False

          Example 4 in prompt template for generating false statements in statement judging task.

2322
          Example 5 in prompt template for generating false statements in statement judging task.
2323
2324      Original Question: For each of the following scenarios, discuss whether profit opportunities
2325      exist from trading in the stock of the firm under the conditions that (1) the market is not
2326      weak form efficient, (2) the market is weak form but not semistrong form efficient, (3) the
2327      market is semistrong form but not strong form efficient, and (4) the market is strong form
2328      efficient. **a.** The stock price has risen steadily each day for the past 30 days. **b.**
2329      The financial statements for a company were released three days ago, and you believe
2330      you’ve uncovered some anomalies in the company’s inventory and cost control reporting
2331      techniques that are causing the firm’s true liquidity strength to be understated. **c.** You
2332
          observe that the senior managers of a company have been buying a lot of the company’s
          stock on the open market over the past week.
2333
2334
          Original Answer:
2335      (a). If the market is not weak form efficient, then this information could be acted on and
2336      a profit earned from following the price trend. Under (2), (3), and (4), this information is
2337      fully impounded in the current price and no abnormal profit opportunity exists.
2338      (b). Under (2), if the market is not semi-strong form efficient, then this information could
2339      be used to buy the stock c̈heapb̈efore the rest of the market discovers the financial statement
2340      anomaly. Since (2) is stronger than (1), both imply that a profit opportunity exists; under (3)
2341      and (4), this information is fully impounded in the current price and no profit opportunity
2342      exists.
2343
          (c). Under (3), if the market is not strong form efficient, then this information could be used
          as a profitable trading strategy, by noting the buying activity of the insiders as a signal that
2344
          the stock is underpriced or that good news is imminent. Since (1) and (2) are weaker than
2345
          (3), all three imply that a profit opportunity exists. Note that this assumes the individual
2346      who sees the insider trading is the only one who sees the trading. If the information about
2347      the trades made by company management is public information, it will be discounted in the
2348      stock price and no profit opportunity exists. Under (4), this information does not signal any
2349      profit opportunity for traders; any pertinent information the manager-insiders may have is
2350      fully reflected in the current share price.
2351
2352      Context: Consider profit opportunities exist from trading in the stock of the firm.
2353
2354
          Statement: In a market that is weak form efficient but not semistrong form efficient,
          a profit could be earned from acting on the information of a stock price that has risen
2355
          steadily each day for the past 30 days.
2356
          Answer: False
2357
2358      Statement: In a market that is strong form efficient, a profit could be earned from
2359      acting on the pertinent information the manager-insiders may have.
2360      Answer: False
2361
2362      Statement: In a market that is semistrong form but not strong form efficient, there is
2363      no profit opportunity on the information that you observe that the senior managers of a
2364      company have been buying a lot of the company’s stock on the open market over the past
2365
          week.
          Answer: False

2448      Prompt template for generating questions in multi-choice question answering task.
2449
2450      Please rewrite a question-answer pair into one or more question(s) with three candidate
2451
          choices. Specifically,
          1. The question and correct answer should be generated from the question and/or answer,
2452
          under a clear and concise wording style. None of the following expressions is allowed in
2453
          the question: (1) unclear pronoun; (2) in/given/according to the chapter/figure/table.
2454      2. There are three candidate choices for the question. The correct answer lies in Choice
2455      (a), and Choice (b) and (c) are both wrong to the question. Choice (a), (b) and (c),
2456      should be independent and mutually exclusive. Noising choices, i.e. (b) and (c), should
2457      share the similar wording and length with the correct answer (a). Choice (b) reflects a
2458      misunderstanding of the original question-answer pair, while Choice (c) is made up by you.
2459      3. You should extract the context of the original question. The context usually introduces
2460      the background of the generated question(s). Note that: (1) the context must NOT be
2461      question; (2) there should NOT be duplicated or contradictory information between the
2462
          context and the statement.
          4. You are allowed to generate two or more questions from one original question-answer
2463
          pair. Under this case, the questions should be independent of each other, with as little
2464
          overlap as possible.

          Example 1 in prompt template for generating questions in multi-choice question answering
2485
          task.
2486
2487      Original Question: Last month, BlueSky Airline announced that it would stretch out its
2488      bill payments to 45 days from 30 days. The reason given was that the company wanted
2489      to c̈ontrol costs and optimize cash flow.T̈he increased payables period will be in effect for
2490      all of the company’s 4,000 suppliers. Why don’t all firms simply increase their payables
2491      periods to shorten their cash cycles?
2492
          Original Answer: They would like to! The payables period is a subject of much ne-
2493
          gotiation, and it is one aspect of the price a firm pays its suppliers. A firm will generally
2494
          negotiate the best possible combination of payables period and price. Typically, suppliers
2495      provide strong financial incentives for rapid payment. This issue is discussed in detail in a
2496      later chapter on credit policy.
2497
2498      Context: Last month, BlueSky Airline announced that it would stretch out its bill
2499      payments to 45 days from 30 days.
2500
2501      Generated Question: Which one of the following choices is one of the reasons of
2502      BlueSky Airline announcement?
2503
          Choices:
          (a) Optimize cash flow
2504
          (b) Increase investment in fixed costs
2505
          (c) Increase sales volume
2506      Correct Answer: a
2507

2511
          Example 2 in prompt template for generating questions in multi-choice question answering
2512
          task.
2513
2514      Original Question: What are the advantages of using the DCF model for determining the
2515      cost of equity capital? What are the disadvantages? What specific piece of information do
2516      you need to find the cost of equity using this model? What are some of the ways in which
2517      you could get this estimate?
2518
          Original Answer: The primary advantage of the DCF model is its simplicity. The
2519
          method is disadvantaged in that (1) the model is applicable only to firms that actually pay
2520
          dividends; many do not; (2) even if a firm does pay dividends, the DCF model requires a
2521      constant dividend growth rate forever; (3) the estimated cost of equity from this method
2522      is very sensitive to changes in g, which is a very uncertain parameter; and (4) the model
2523      does not explicitly consider risk, although risk is implicitly considered to the extent that
2524      the market has impounded the relevant risk of the stock into its market price. While the
2525      share price and most recent dividend can be observed in the market, the dividend growth
2526      rate must be estimated. Two common methods of estimating g are to use analysts’ earnings
2527      and payout forecasts or to determine some appropriate average historical g from the firm’s
2528      available data.
2529
          Context: The DCF model have advantages and disadvantages for determining the
2530
          cost of equity capital.
2531
2532      Generated Question: Which one of the following advantages do the DCF model have?
2533      Choices:
2534      (a) Simple calculation
2535      (b) Applicable for firms that do not pay dividends
2536      (c) Insensitivity to the financial environment
2537      Correct Answer: a

       Under review as a conference paper at ICLR 2025

          Example 3 in prompt template for generating questions in multi-choice question answering
2539
          task.
2540
2541      Original Question: ’When a bank is negotiating currency swaps, it should try to ensure
2542      that it is receiving the lower interest rate currency from a company with a low credit risk.’
2543      Explain.
2544
2545      Original Answer: As time passes there is a tendency for the currency which has the
2546
          lower interest rate to strengthen. This means that a swap where we are receiving this
          currency will tend to move in the money (i.e., have a positive value). Similarly a swap
2547
          where we are paying the currency will tend to move out of the money (i.e., have a negative
2548
          value). From this it follows that our expected exposure on the swap where we are receiving
2549      the low-interest currency is much greater than our expected exposure on the swap where we
2550      are receiving the high-interest currency. We should therefore look for counterparties with
2551      a low credit risk on the side of the swap where we are receiving the low-interest currency.
2552      On the other side of the swap we are far less concerned about the creditworthiness of the
2553      counterparty.
2554
2555      Context: A bank is negotiating currency swaps.
2556
2557
          Generated Question: Which one of the following actions should it consider?
          Choices:
2558
          (a) Seek counterparties with low credit risk where the bank is receiving the low-interest
2559
          currency
2560      (b) Seek counterparties with high credit risk where the bank is receiving the low-interest
2561      currency
2562      (c) Seek counterparties with low credit risk where the bank is receiving the high-interest
2563      currency
2564      Correct Answer: a
2565

          Example 4 in prompt template for generating questions in multi-choice question answering
2593
          task.
2594
2595      Original Question: How can bank behavior and the Fed’s behavior cause money supply
2596      growth to be precyclical (rising in booms and falling in recessions)?
2597
2598      Original Answer: Bank behavior can lead to procyclical money growth because when
2599      interest rates rise in a boom, they decrease excess reserves and increase their borrowing
2600
          from the Fed, both of which lead to a higher money supply. Similarly, when interest rates
          fall in a recession, they increase excess reserves and decrease their borrowing from the Fed,
2601
          leading to a lower money supply. The result is that the money supply will tend to grow
2602
          faster in booms and slower in recessions–it is procyclical. Fed behavior also can lead to
2603      procyclical money growth because (as the answer to problem 1 indicates) an interest-rate
2604      target can lead to a slower rate of growth of the money supply during recessions and a more
2605      rapid rate of growth during booms.
2606
2607      Context: Bank behavior and the Fed’s behavior can cause money supply growth to
2608      be precyclica.
2609
2610      Generated Question: Which one of the following bank and/or the Fed’s behaviours
2611
          would happen when interest rates rise in a boom?
          Choices:
2612
          (a) Banks increase their borrowings from the Fed
2613
          (b) Banks increase excess reserves
2614      (c) The Fed’s make positive announcements
2615      Correct Answer: a
2616
2617      Generated Question: Which one of the following bank and/or the Fed’s behaviours
2618      would happen when interest rates rise in a recession?
2619      Choices:
2620      (a) Banks decrease their borrowings from the Fed
2621      (b) Banks decrease excess reserves
2622
          (c) The Fed’s make positive announcements
          Correct Answer: a

          Example 3 in prompt template for generating questions in financial calculation task.
2917
2918      Original Question: You want to buy a new sports coupe for $61,800, and the finance office
2919      at the dealership has quoted you a 7.4 percent APR loan for 60 months to buy the car. What
2920      will your monthly payments be? What is the effective annual rate on this loan?
2921
2922      Original Answer: We first need to find the annuity payment. We have the PVA, the
2923      length of the annuity, and the interest rate. Using the PVA equation:
2924
2925                                   P V A = C([1 − [1/(1 + r)]t ]r)
2926
2927
2928                         $61, 800 = C[1 − [1/[1 + (.074/12)]60 ]](.074/12)]
2929
2930      Solving for the payment, we get:
2931
2932                                C = $61, 800/50.02385 = $1, 235.41
2933
2934      To find the EAR, we use the EAR equation:
2935
2936                                   EAR = [1 + (AP R/m)]m − 1
2937
2938
2939                               EAR = [1 + (.074/12)]12 − 1 = .0766
2940
2941
2942      Context: You want to buy a new sports coupe for $61,800, and the finance office at
2943      the dealership has quoted you a 7.4 percent APR loan for 60 months to buy the car.
2944
2945      Generated Question: What will your monthly payments be? (Unit: dollar)
2946
          Answer: 1235.41
2947
          Generated Question: What is the effective annual rate on this loan?
2948
          Answer: 0.0766

2970
          Example 4 in prompt template for generating questions in financial calculation task.
2971
2972      Original Question: What is the value of an investment that pays $7,500 every other year
2973      forever, if the first payment occurs one year from today and the discount rate is 11 percent
2974      compounded daily? What is the value today if the first payment occurs four years from
2975      today?
2976
2977      Original Answer: The cash flows in this problem occur every two years, so we need
2978      to find the effective two year rate. One way to find the effective two year rate is to use an
2979      equation similar to the EAR, except use the number of days in two years as the exponent.
2980
          (We use the number of days in two years since it is daily compounding; if monthly com-
          pounding was assumed, we would use the number of months in two years.) So, the effective
2981                                                                        [
2982      two-year interest rate is: Effective 2-year rate = [1 + (.11/365)] 365(2)] − 1 = .2460
2983
          We can use this interest rate to find the PV of the perpetuity. Doing so, we find:
          PV = $7, 500/.2460 = $30, 483.41
2984
          This is an important point: Remember that the PV equation for a perpetuity (and an
2985
          ordinary annuity) tells you the PV one period before the first cash flow. In this problem,
2986      since the cash flows are two years apart, we have found the value of the perpetuity one
2987      period (two years) before the first payment, which is one year ago. We need to compound
2988      this value for one year to find the value today. The value of the cash flows today is:
2989      PV = $30, 483.41(1 + .11/365)365 = $34, 027.40 The second part of the question assumes
2990      the perpetuity cash flows begin in four years. In this case, when we use the PV of a
2991      perpetuity equation, we find the value of the perpetuity two years from today. So, the
2992      value of these cash flows today is: PV = $30, 483.41/(1 + .11/365)2(365) = $24, 464.32
2993      Context: An investment pays $7,500 every other year forever. The discount rate is 11
2994      percent compounded daily.
2995
          Generated Question: What is the value of the investment if the first payment occurs
2996
          one year from today? (Unit: dollar)
2997
          Answer: 34027.40
2998
2999      Generated Question: What is the value of the investment if the first payment occurs
3000      four year from today? (Unit: dollar)
3001      Answer: 24464.32

3024
          Example 5 in prompt template for generating questions in financial calculation task.
3025
3026      Original Question: An investment offers $4,600 per year for 15 years, with the first payment
3027      occurring one year from now. If the required return is 8 percent, what is the value of the
3028      investment? What would the value be if the payments occurred for 40 years? For 75 years?
3029      Forever?
3030
3031      Original Answer: To find the PVA, we use the equation:
3032      P V A = C([1–[1/(1 + r)]t ]/r)
3033      PVA@15 yrs: P V A = $4, 600[[1–(1/1.08)15 ]/.08] = $39, 373.60
3034
          PVA@40 yrs: P V A = $4, 600[[1–(1/1.08)40 ]/.08] = $54, 853.22
          PVA@75 yrs: P V A = $4, 600[[1–(1/1.08)75 ]/.08] = $57, 320.99
3035
          To find the PV of a perpetuity, we use the equation:
3036
          P V = C/r
3037      P V = $4, 600/.08 = $57, 500.00
3038      Notice that as the length of the annuity payments increases, the present value of the annuity
3039      approaches the present value of the perpetuity. The present value of the 75 year annuity and
3040      the present value of the perpetuity imply that the value today of all perpetuity payments
3041      beyond 75 years is only $179.01.
3042
3043      Context: An investment offers $4,600 per year for 15 years, with the first payment
3044      occurring one year from now. The required return is 8 percent
3045
          Generated Question: What is the value of the investment? (Unit: dollar)
3046
          Answer: 39373.60
3047
3048      Generated Question: If the payments occurred for 40 years, what is the value of the
3049      investment? (Unit: dollar)
3050      Answer: 54853.22
3051
3052      Generated Question: If the payments occurred for 75 years, what is the value of the
3053      investment? (Unit: dollar)
3054      Answer: 57320.99
3055
3056
          Generated Question: If the payments occurred forever, what is the value of the in-
          vestment? (Unit: dollar)
3057
          Answer: 57500.00

       G.2.4    P ROMPT FOR M ATHEMATICAL C APABILITY A NNOTATION
3079
3080
          Prompt template for asking gpt-4o to annotate mathematical reasoning types to calculating
3081      questions.
3082
3083      Below are seven reasoning abilities required in solving math problems:
3084      1. Numeric Commonsense: It involves intuitive understanding of daily numerical concepts,
3085      including understanding time differences, numerical judgment, and estimates. It covers
3086      temporal reasoning, spatial numeric assessments, and practical uses like budgeting and time
3087      reading.
3088      2. Logical Reasoning: It focuses on critical thinking and deduction from provided infor-
3089
          mation, including pattern recognition, sequence understanding, predictions, and statement
          evaluation. Key components include premises, conclusions, and the use of abstract
3090
          reasoning.
3091
          3. Statistical Reasoning: It focuses on data interpretation and analysis, including measures
3092      (mean, median, mode), dispersion metrics (standard deviation, range), probability concepts,
3093      regression, correlation, and data inferences. It also identifies trends, outliers, and patterns.
3094      4. Arithmetic Reasoning: It covers the fundamental operations such as addition, subtraction,
3095      multiplication, division, and understanding of number properties. It may also include the
3096      ability to interpret numerical data in different forms.
3097      5. Algebraic Reasoning: It encompasses understanding variables, equations, and the
3098      manipulation of expressions with polynomials and exponents. It also covers solving simple
3099      to complex equations, and grasping functions, their properties, and graphical depictions.
3100
          6. Geometry Reasoning: It emphasizes spatial understanding, analysis of 2D and 3D
          figures, and reasoning about their shapes, sizes, and relationships. It includes symmetry,
3101
          congruency, similarity, area, volume, and transformations.
3102
          7. Scientific Reasoning: It deals with the application of mathematical concepts in scientific
3103      contexts. This includes scientific notations, formula use, understanding rates, proportions,
3104      and percentages in practical situations, and problem-solving in scientific inquiries.
3105
3106      Question: { question }
3107      Answer: { answer }
3108      Above is a calculating question along with its answer in finance domain. Plase label this
3109      question with at most two reasoning abilities defined above. You are NOT allowed to create
3110      other abilities. You should output your final answer with ’Therefore, my answer is’.
3111
          Let’s think step by step.

3168   H    E THICS AND S OCIETAL I MPACT
3169
3170   We envision XF IN B ENCH as a comprehensive benchmark designed to assist researchers in eval-
3171
       uating the performance of their models within the finance domain. By offering a robust evalua-
       tion framework, XF IN B ENCH aims to drive advancements in foundational models for the research
3172
       community, providing valuable insights into critical model capabilities such as temporal reasoning,
3173
       future forecasting, scenario planning, numerical modeling, and cross-modal reasoning.
3174
3175   For constructing examples in XF IN B ENCH and finance terms for the knowledge bank, we primarily
3176   rely on textbooks that are openly available on the internet. Our annotators strictly adhere to copyright
3177
       and licensing regulations, ensuring that data from sources prohibiting copying or redistribution is
       excluded. Furthermore, during the automated annotation and human quality validation processes for
3178
       examples in XF IN B ENCH, we implement rigorous ethical guidelines to prevent biased content and
3179
       safeguard against the inclusion of private data.
